    15	package caddyfile
    16	
    17	import (
    18	        "bytes"
    19	        "fmt"
    20	        "io"
    21	        "os"
    22	        "path/filepath"
    23	        "strings"

    25	        "go.uber.org/zap"

    27	        "github.com/caddyserver/caddy/v2"

    29	
    30	// Parse parses the input just enough to group tokens, in
    31	// order, by server block. No further parsing is performed.
    32	// Server blocks are returned in the order in which they appear.
    33	// Directives that do not appear in validDirectives will cause
    34	// an error. If you do not want to check for valid directives,
    35	// pass in nil instead.
    36	//
    37	// Environment variables in {$ENVIRONMENT_VARIABLE} notation
    38	// will be replaced before parsing begins.
    39	func Parse(filename string, input []byte) ([]ServerBlock, error) {
    40	        // unfortunately, we must copy the input because parsing must
    41	        // remain a read-only operation, but we have to expand environment
    42	        // variables before we parse, which changes the underlying array (#4422)
    43	        inputCopy := make([]byte, len(input))
    44	        copy(inputCopy, input)
    45	
    46	        tokens, err := allTokens(filename, inputCopy)
    47	        if err != nil {
    48	                return nil, err
    49	        }
    50	        p := parser{
    51	                Dispenser: NewDispenser(tokens),
    52	                importGraph: importGraph{
    53	                        nodes: make(map[string]struct{}),
    54	                        edges: make(adjacency),
    55	                },
    56	        }
    57	        return p.parseAll()
    58	}
    59	
    60	// allTokens lexes the entire input, but does not parse it.
    61	// It returns all the tokens from the input, unstructured
    62	// and in order. It may mutate input as it expands env vars.
    63	func allTokens(filename string, input []byte) ([]Token, error) {
    64	        return Tokenize(replaceEnvVars(input), filename)
    65	}
    66	
    67	// replaceEnvVars replaces all occurrences of environment variables.
    68	// It mutates the underlying array and returns the updated slice.
    69	func replaceEnvVars(input []byte) []byte {
    70	        var offset int
    71	        for {
    72	                begin := bytes.Index(input[offset:], spanOpen)
    73	                if begin < 0 {
    74	                        break
    75	                }
    76	                begin += offset // make beginning relative to input, not offset
    77	                end := bytes.Index(input[begin+len(spanOpen):], spanClose)
    78	                if end < 0 {
    79	                        break
    80	                }
    81	                end += begin + len(spanOpen) // make end relative to input, not begin
    82	
    83	                // get the name; if there is no name, skip it
    84	                envString := input[begin+len(spanOpen) : end]
    85	                if len(envString) == 0 {
    86	                        offset = end + len(spanClose)
    87	                        continue
    88	                }
    89	
    90	                // split the string into a key and an optional default
    91	                envParts := strings.SplitN(string(envString), envVarDefaultDelimiter, 2)
    92	
    93	                // do a lookup for the env var, replace with the default if not found
    94	                envVarValue, found := os.LookupEnv(envParts[0])
    95	                if !found && len(envParts) == 2 {
    96	                        envVarValue = envParts[1]
    97	                }
    98	
    99	                // get the value of the environment variable
   100	                // note that this causes one-level deep chaining
   101	                envVarBytes := []byte(envVarValue)
   102	
   103	                // splice in the value
   104	                input = append(input[:begin],
   105	                        append(envVarBytes, input[end+len(spanClose):]...)...)
   106	
   107	                // continue at the end of the replacement
   108	                offset = begin + len(envVarBytes)
   109	        }
   110	        return input
   111	}
   112	
   113	type parser struct {
   114	        *Dispenser
   115	        block           ServerBlock // current server block being parsed
   116	        eof             bool        // if we encounter a valid EOF in a hard place
   117	        definedSnippets map[string][]Token
   118	        nesting         int
   119	        importGraph     importGraph
   120	}
   121	
   122	func (p *parser) parseAll() ([]ServerBlock, error) {
   123	        var blocks []ServerBlock
   124	
   125	        for p.Next() {
   126	                err := p.parseOne()
   127	                if err != nil {
   128	                        return blocks, err
   129	                }
   130	                if len(p.block.Keys) > 0 || len(p.block.Segments) > 0 {
   131	                        blocks = append(blocks, p.block)
   132	                }
   133	                if p.nesting > 0 {
   134	                        return blocks, p.EOFErr()
   135	                }
   136	        }
   137	
   138	        return blocks, nil
   139	}
   140	
   141	func (p *parser) parseOne() error {
   142	        p.block = ServerBlock{}
   143	        return p.begin()
   144	}
   145	
   146	func (p *parser) begin() error {
   147	        if len(p.tokens) == 0 {
   148	                return nil
   149	        }
   150	
   151	        err := p.addresses()
   152	        if err != nil {
   153	                return err
   154	        }
   155	
   156	        if p.eof {
   157	                // this happens if the Caddyfile consists of only
   158	                // a line of addresses and nothing else
   159	                return nil
   160	        }
   161	
   162	        if ok, name := p.isNamedRoute(); ok {
   163	                // we just need a dummy leading token to ease parsing later
   164	                nameToken := p.Token()
   165	                nameToken.Text = name
   166	
   167	                // named routes only have one key, the route name
   168	                p.block.Keys = []Token{nameToken}
   169	                p.block.IsNamedRoute = true
   170	
   171	                // get all the tokens from the block, including the braces
   172	                tokens, err := p.blockTokens(true)
   173	                if err != nil {
   174	                        return err
   175	                }
   176	                tokens = append([]Token{nameToken}, tokens...)
   177	                p.block.Segments = []Segment{tokens}
   178	                return nil
   179	        }
   180	
   181	        if ok, name := p.isSnippet(); ok {
   182	                if p.definedSnippets == nil {
   183	                        p.definedSnippets = map[string][]Token{}
   184	                }
   185	                if _, found := p.definedSnippets[name]; found {
   186	                        return p.Errf("redeclaration of previously declared snippet %s", name)
   187	                }
   188	                // consume all tokens til matched close brace
   189	                tokens, err := p.blockTokens(false)
   190	                if err != nil {
   191	                        return err
   192	                }
   193	                // Just as we need to track which file the token comes from, we need to
   194	                // keep track of which snippet the token comes from. This is helpful
   195	                // in tracking import cycles across files/snippets by namespacing them.
   196	                // Without this, we end up with false-positives in cycle-detection.
   197	                for k, v := range tokens {
   198	                        v.snippetName = name
   199	                        tokens[k] = v
   200	                }
   201	                p.definedSnippets[name] = tokens
   202	                // empty block keys so we don't save this block as a real server.
   203	                p.block.Keys = nil
   204	                return nil
   205	        }
   206	
   207	        return p.blockContents()
   208	}
   209	
   210	func (p *parser) addresses() error {
   211	        var expectingAnother bool
   212	
   213	        for {
   214	                value := p.Val()
   215	                token := p.Token()
   216	
   217	                // Reject request matchers if trying to define them globally
   218	                if strings.HasPrefix(value, "@") {
   219	                        return p.Errf("request matchers may not be defined globally, they must be in a site block; found %s", value)
   220	                }
   221	
   222	                // Special case: import directive replaces tokens during parse-time
   223	                if value == "import" && p.isNewLine() {
   224	                        err := p.doImport(0)
   225	                        if err != nil {
   226	                                return err
   227	                        }
   228	                        continue
   229	                }
   230	
   231	                // Open brace definitely indicates end of addresses
   232	                if value == "{" {
   233	                        if expectingAnother {
   234	                                return p.Errf("Expected another address but had '%s' - check for extra comma", value)
   235	                        }
   236	                        // Mark this server block as being defined with braces.
   237	                        // This is used to provide a better error message when
   238	                        // the user may have tried to define two server blocks
   239	                        // without having used braces, which are required in
   240	                        // that case.
   241	                        p.block.HasBraces = true
   242	                        break
   243	                }
   244	
   245	                // Users commonly forget to place a space between the address and the '{'
   246	                if strings.HasSuffix(value, "{") {
   247	                        return p.Errf("Site addresses cannot end with a curly brace: '%s' - put a space between the token and the brace", value)
   248	                }
   249	
   250	                if value != "" { // empty token possible if user typed ""
   251	                        // Trailing comma indicates another address will follow, which
   252	                        // may possibly be on the next line
   253	                        if value[len(value)-1] == ',' {
   254	                                value = value[:len(value)-1]
   255	                                expectingAnother = true
   256	                        } else {
   257	                                expectingAnother = false // but we may still see another one on this line
   258	                        }
   259	
   260	                        // If there's a comma here, it's probably because they didn't use a space
   261	                        // between their two domains, e.g. "foo.com,bar.com", which would not be
   262	                        // parsed as two separate site addresses.
   263	                        if strings.Contains(value, ",") {
   264	                                return p.Errf("Site addresses cannot contain a comma ',': '%s' - put a space after the comma to separate site addresses", value)
   265	                        }
   266	
   267	                        // After the above, a comma surrounded by spaces would result
   268	                        // in an empty token which we should ignore
   269	                        if value != "" {
   270	                                // Add the token as a site address
   271	                                token.Text = value
   272	                                p.block.Keys = append(p.block.Keys, token)
   273	                        }
   274	                }
   275	
   276	                // Advance token and possibly break out of loop or return error
   277	                hasNext := p.Next()
   278	                if expectingAnother && !hasNext {
   279	                        return p.EOFErr()
   280	                }
   281	                if !hasNext {
   282	                        p.eof = true
   283	                        break // EOF
   284	                }
   285	                if !expectingAnother && p.isNewLine() {
   286	                        break
   287	                }
   288	        }
   289	
   290	        return nil
   291	}
   292	
   293	func (p *parser) blockContents() error {
   294	        errOpenCurlyBrace := p.openCurlyBrace()
   295	        if errOpenCurlyBrace != nil {
   296	                // single-server configs don't need curly braces
   297	                p.cursor--
   298	        }
   299	
   300	        err := p.directives()
   301	        if err != nil {
   302	                return err
   303	        }
   304	
   305	        // only look for close curly brace if there was an opening
   306	        if errOpenCurlyBrace == nil {
   307	                err = p.closeCurlyBrace()
   308	                if err != nil {
   309	                        return err
   310	                }
   311	        }
   312	
   313	        return nil
   314	}
   315	
   316	// directives parses through all the lines for directives
   317	// and it expects the next token to be the first
   318	// directive. It goes until EOF or closing curly brace
   319	// which ends the server block.
   320	func (p *parser) directives() error {
   321	        for p.Next() {
   322	                // end of server block
   323	                if p.Val() == "}" {
   324	                        // p.nesting has already been decremented
   325	                        break
   326	                }
   327	
   328	                // special case: import directive replaces tokens during parse-time
   329	                if p.Val() == "import" {
   330	                        err := p.doImport(1)
   331	                        if err != nil {
   332	                                return err
   333	                        }
   334	                        p.cursor-- // cursor is advanced when we continue, so roll back one more
   335	                        continue
   336	                }
   337	
   338	                // normal case: parse a directive as a new segment
   339	                // (a "segment" is a line which starts with a directive
   340	                // and which ends at the end of the line or at the end of
   341	                // the block that is opened at the end of the line)
   342	                if err := p.directive(); err != nil {
   343	                        return err
   344	                }
   345	        }
   346	
   347	        return nil
   348	}
   349	
   350	// doImport swaps out the import directive and its argument
   351	// (a total of 2 tokens) with the tokens in the specified file
   352	// or globbing pattern. When the function returns, the cursor
   353	// is on the token before where the import directive was. In
   354	// other words, call Next() to access the first token that was
   355	// imported.
   356	func (p *parser) doImport(nesting int) error {
   357	        // syntax checks
   358	        if !p.NextArg() {
   359	                return p.ArgErr()
   360	        }
   361	        importPattern := p.Val()
   362	        if importPattern == "" {
   363	                return p.Err("Import requires a non-empty filepath")
   364	        }
   365	
   366	        // grab remaining args as placeholder replacements
   367	        args := p.RemainingArgs()
   368	
   369	        // set up a replacer for non-variadic args replacement
   370	        repl := makeArgsReplacer(args)
   371	
   372	        // grab all the tokens (if it exists) from within a block that follows the import
   373	        var blockTokens []Token
   374	        for currentNesting := p.Nesting(); p.NextBlock(currentNesting); {
   375	                blockTokens = append(blockTokens, p.Token())
   376	        }
   377	        // initialize with size 1
   378	        blockMapping := make(map[string][]Token, 1)
   379	        if len(blockTokens) > 0 {
   380	                // use such tokens to create a new dispenser, and then use it to parse each block
   381	                bd := NewDispenser(blockTokens)
   382	                for bd.Next() {
   383	                        // see if we can grab a key
   384	                        var currentMappingKey string
   385	                        if bd.Val() == "{" {
   386	                                return p.Err("anonymous blocks are not supported")
   387	                        }
   388	                        currentMappingKey = bd.Val()
   389	                        currentMappingTokens := []Token{}
   390	                        // read all args until end of line / {
   391	                        if bd.NextArg() {
   392	                                currentMappingTokens = append(currentMappingTokens, bd.Token())
   393	                                for bd.NextArg() {
   394	                                        currentMappingTokens = append(currentMappingTokens, bd.Token())
   395	                                }
   396	                                // TODO(elee1766): we don't enter another mapping here because it's annoying to extract the { and } properly.
   397	                                // maybe someone can do that in the future
   398	                        } else {
   399	                                // attempt to enter a block and add tokens to the currentMappingTokens
   400	                                for mappingNesting := bd.Nesting(); bd.NextBlock(mappingNesting); {
   401	                                        currentMappingTokens = append(currentMappingTokens, bd.Token())
   402	                                }
   403	                        }
   404	                        blockMapping[currentMappingKey] = currentMappingTokens
   405	                }
   406	        }
   407	
   408	        // splice out the import directive and its arguments
   409	        // (2 tokens, plus the length of args)
   410	        tokensBefore := p.tokens[:p.cursor-1-len(args)-len(blockTokens)]
   411	        tokensAfter := p.tokens[p.cursor+1:]
   412	        var importedTokens []Token
   413	        var nodes []string
   414	
   415	        // first check snippets. That is a simple, non-recursive replacement
   416	        if p.definedSnippets != nil && p.definedSnippets[importPattern] != nil {
   417	                importedTokens = p.definedSnippets[importPattern]
   418	                if len(importedTokens) > 0 {
   419	                        // just grab the first one
   420	                        nodes = append(nodes, fmt.Sprintf("%s:%s", importedTokens[0].File, importedTokens[0].snippetName))
   421	                }
   422	        } else {
   423	                // make path relative to the file of the _token_ being processed rather
   424	                // than current working directory (issue #867) and then use glob to get
   425	                // list of matching filenames
   426	                absFile, err := caddy.FastAbs(p.Dispenser.File())
   427	                if err != nil {
   428	                        return p.Errf("Failed to get absolute path of file: %s: %v", p.Dispenser.File(), err)
   429	                }
   430	
   431	                var matches []string
   432	                var globPattern string
   433	                if !filepath.IsAbs(importPattern) {
   434	                        globPattern = filepath.Join(filepath.Dir(absFile), importPattern)
   435	                } else {
   436	                        globPattern = importPattern
   437	                }
   438	                if strings.Count(globPattern, "*") > 1 || strings.Count(globPattern, "?") > 1 ||
   439	                        (strings.Contains(globPattern, "[") && strings.Contains(globPattern, "]")) {
   440	                        // See issue #2096 - a pattern with many glob expansions can hang for too long
   441	                        return p.Errf("Glob pattern may only contain one wildcard (*), but has others: %s", globPattern)
   442	                }
   443	                matches, err = filepath.Glob(globPattern)
   444	                if err != nil {
   445	                        return p.Errf("Failed to use import pattern %s: %v", importPattern, err)
   446	                }
   447	                if len(matches) == 0 {
   448	                        if strings.ContainsAny(globPattern, "*?[]") {
   449	                                caddy.Log().Warn("No files matching import glob pattern", zap.String("pattern", importPattern))
   450	                        } else {
   451	                                return p.Errf("File to import not found: %s", importPattern)
   452	                        }
   453	                } else {
   454	                        // See issue #5295 - should skip any files that start with a . when iterating over them.
   455	                        sep := string(filepath.Separator)
   456	                        segGlobPattern := strings.Split(globPattern, sep)
   457	                        if strings.HasPrefix(segGlobPattern[len(segGlobPattern)-1], "*") {
   458	                                var tmpMatches []string
   459	                                for _, m := range matches {
   460	                                        seg := strings.Split(m, sep)
   461	                                        if !strings.HasPrefix(seg[len(seg)-1], ".") {
   462	                                                tmpMatches = append(tmpMatches, m)
   463	                                        }
   464	                                }
   465	                                matches = tmpMatches
   466	                        }
   467	                }
   468	
   469	                // collect all the imported tokens
   470	                for _, importFile := range matches {
   471	                        newTokens, err := p.doSingleImport(importFile)
   472	                        if err != nil {
   473	                                return err
   474	                        }
   475	                        importedTokens = append(importedTokens, newTokens...)
   476	                }
   477	                nodes = matches
   478	        }
   479	
   480	        nodeName := p.File()
   481	        if p.Token().snippetName != "" {
   482	                nodeName += fmt.Sprintf(":%s", p.Token().snippetName)
   483	        }
   484	        p.importGraph.addNode(nodeName)
   485	        p.importGraph.addNodes(nodes)
   486	        if err := p.importGraph.addEdges(nodeName, nodes); err != nil {
   487	                p.importGraph.removeNodes(nodes)
   488	                return err
   489	        }
   490	
   491	        // copy the tokens so we don't overwrite p.definedSnippets
   492	        tokensCopy := make([]Token, 0, len(importedTokens))
   493	
   494	        var (
   495	                maybeSnippet   bool
   496	                maybeSnippetId bool
   497	                index          int
   498	        )
   499	
   500	        // run the argument replacer on the tokens
   501	        // golang for range slice return a copy of value
   502	        // similarly, append also copy value
   503	        for i, token := range importedTokens {
   504	                // update the token's imports to refer to import directive filename, line number and snippet name if there is one
   505	                if token.snippetName != "" {
   506	                        token.imports = append(token.imports, fmt.Sprintf("%s:%d (import %s)", p.File(), p.Line(), token.snippetName))
   507	                } else {
   508	                        token.imports = append(token.imports, fmt.Sprintf("%s:%d (import)", p.File(), p.Line()))
   509	                }
   510	
   511	                // naive way of determine snippets, as snippets definition can only follow name + block
   512	                // format, won't check for nesting correctness or any other error, that's what parser does.
   513	                if !maybeSnippet && nesting == 0 {
   514	                        // first of the line
   515	                        if i == 0 || isNextOnNewLine(tokensCopy[i-1], token) {
   516	                                index = 0
   517	                        } else {
   518	                                index++
   519	                        }
   520	
   521	                        if index == 0 && len(token.Text) >= 3 && strings.HasPrefix(token.Text, "(") && strings.HasSuffix(token.Text, ")") {
   522	                                maybeSnippetId = true
   523	                        }
   524	                }
   525	
   526	                switch token.Text {
   527	                case "{":
   528	                        nesting++
   529	                        if index == 1 && maybeSnippetId && nesting == 1 {
   530	                                maybeSnippe<response clipped><NOTE>To save on context only part of this file has been shown to you. You should retry this tool after you have searched inside the file with `grep -n` in order to find the line numbers of what you are looking for.</NOTE>

Now let me analyze the problem more carefully by looking at how the import block parsing works:

1. When we have an import with a block like:
   ```caddyfile
   import site test.domain {
     reverse_proxy http://192.168.1.1:8080 { 
       header_up Host {host}

     }
   }
   ```

3. In the code at lines 385-386, it checks if the first token is "{" and returns an error if so.

The problem is that this check is too restrictive. It should only reject anonymous blocks (blocks that start with `{` without a directive name), but it should allow blocks that have a directive name followed by a block.

However, looking at the logic, this check is meant to prevent anonymous blocks (blocks that don\'t have a directive name), but the implementation is flawed.\n\nLet me trace through what\'s happening:\n\n1. When we have `import site test.domain { reverse_proxy ... { ... } }`, the parser collects the tokens from `reverse_proxy` to the closing `}`.\n\n2. Now I understand the issue. The code is trying to parse the block after the `import` directive, but it's incorrectly rejecting any block that contains a `{` as the first token. However, looking at the logic, this check is meant to prevent anonymous blocks (blocks that don't have a directive name), but the implementation is flawed.

Let me trace through what's happening:

1. When we have `import site test.domain { reverse_proxy ... { ... } }`, the parser collects the tokens from `reverse_proxy` to the closing `}`.

2. It then creates a new dispenser `bd` with these tokens and starts iterating through them.

3. The issue is that when it encounters the `{` after `reverse_proxy`, it incorrectly identifies this as an "anonymous block" because `bd.Val()` returns `{`.

However, this is NOT an anonymous block. An anonymous block would be something like:
```caddyfile
import site test.domain {
  {  # This would be an anonymous block
    header_up Host {host}
  }
}
```

The current code should allow blocks that have a directive name followed by a block. The issue is that the check at line 385-386 is too broad - it rejects any block that starts with `{`, but it should only reject blocks that are truly anonymous (i.e., blocks that don't have a directive name).

Let me look at how the block tokens are structured:

   167	func (d *Dispenser) NextBlock(initialNestingLevel int) bool {
   168	        if d.nesting > initialNestingLevel {
   169	                if !d.Next() {
   170	                        return false // should be EOF error
   171	                }
   172	                if d.Val() == "}" && !d.nextOnSameLine() {
   173	                        d.nesting--
   174	                } else if d.Val() == "{" && !d.nextOnSameLine() {
   175	                        d.nesting++
   176	                }
   177	                return d.nesting > initialNestingLevel
   178	        }
   179	        if !d.nextOnSameLine() { // block must open on same line
   180	                return false
   181	        }
   182	        if d.Val() != "{" {
   183	                d.cursor-- // roll back if not opening brace
   184	                return false
   185	        }
   186	        d.Next() // consume open curly brace
   187	        if d.Val() == "}" {
   188	                return false // open and then closed right away
   189	        }
   190	        d.nesting++
   191	        return true
   192	}
   193

Now I need to understand what's happening. Let me examine the issue more closely. The problem is that when parsing the import directive block, the code encounters an open curly brace `{` and immediately returns an error saying "anonymous blocks are not supported". However, this is not an anonymous block - it's a properly named directive block.

Let me trace through what happens:

1. The import directive is parsed with a block content after it
2. The block tokens are collected (lines 372-376)
3. A new dispenser `bd` is created from these block tokens
4. The dispenser iterates through the tokens and encounters `{` as the first token in line 385
5. It immediately returns an error

The issue is that the code assumes that if the first token is `{`, it's an anonymous block, but in this case, the tokens are from within the import block, which should contain a directive followed by its block.

   350	// doImport swaps out the import directive and its argument
   351	// (a total of 2 tokens) with the tokens in the specified file
   352	// or globbing pattern. When the function returns, the cursor
   353	// is on the token before where the import directive was. In
   354	// other words, call Next() to access the first token that was
   355	// imported.
   356	func (p *parser) doImport(nesting int) error {
   357	        // syntax checks
   358	        if !p.NextArg() {
   359	                return p.ArgErr()
   360	        }
   361	        importPattern := p.Val()
   362	        if importPattern == "" {
   363	                return p.Err("Import requires a non-empty filepath")
   364	        }
   365	
   366	        // grab remaining args as placeholder replacements
   367	        args := p.RemainingArgs()
   368	
   369	        // set up a replacer for non-variadic args replacement
   370	        repl := makeArgsReplacer(args)
   371	
   372	        // grab all the tokens (if it exists) from within a block that follows the import
   373	        var blockTokens []Token
   374	        for currentNesting := p.Nesting(); p.NextBlock(currentNesting); {
   375	                blockTokens = append(blockTokens, p.Token())
   376	        }
   377	        // initialize with size 1
   378	        blockMapping := make(map[string][]Token, 1)
   379	        if len(blockTokens) > 0 {
   380	                // use such tokens to create a new dispenser, and then use it to parse each block
   381	                bd := NewDispenser(blockTokens)
   382	                for bd.Next() {
   383	                        // see if we can grab a key
   384	                        var currentMappingKey string
   385	                        if bd.Val() == "{" {
   386	                                return p.Err("anonymous blocks are not supported")
   387	                        }
   388	                        currentMappingKey = bd.Val()
   389	                        currentMappingTokens := []Token{}
   390	                        // read all args until end of line / {
   391	                        if bd.NextArg() {
   392	                                currentMappingTokens = append(currentMappingTokens, bd.Token())
   393	                                for bd.NextArg() {
   394	                                        currentMappingTokens = append(currentMappingTokens, bd.Token())
   395	                                }
   396	                                // TODO(elee1766): we don't enter another mapping here because it's annoying to extract the { and } properly.
   397	                                // maybe someone can do that in the future
   398	                        } else {
   399	                                // attempt to enter a block and add tokens to the currentMappingTokens
   400	                                for mappingNesting := bd.Nesting(); bd.NextBlock(mappingNesting); {
   401	                                        currentMappingTokens = append(currentMappingTokens, bd.Token())
   402	                                }
   403	                        }
   404	                        blockMapping[currentMappingKey] = currentMappingTokens
   405	                }
   406	        }
   407	
   408	        // splice out the import directive and its arguments
   409	        // (2 tokens, plus the length of args)
   410	        tokensBefore := p.tokens[:p.cursor-1-len(args)-len(blockTokens)]

Now I understand the issue. Let me analyze the problem:

1. When parsing an import statement with a block like:
   ```caddyfile
   import site test.domain {
     reverse_proxy http://192.168.1.1:8080 { 
       header_up Host {host}
       header_up X-Real-IP {remote_host}
     }
   }
   ```

2. The parser extracts the block content after `import site test.domain {` and creates a `blockMapping`.

3. The issue is on line 385-387 where if the first token in the block is `{`, it errors with "anonymous blocks are not supported".

4. However, in the case of a directive with nested blocks (like `reverse_proxy` with its own `{...}`), the tokens start with `reverse_proxy`, followed by arguments, and then `{`.

🎬 ACTION
str_replace_editor create /testbed/test_token_logic.go --file_text 'package main

import (
	"fmt"
	"github.com/caddyserver/caddy/v2/caddyconfig/caddyfile"
)

func main() {
	// Test just the block content that would be extracted
	blockContent := `reverse_proxy http://192.168.1.1:8080 { 
    header_up Host {host}
    header_up X-Real-IP {remote_host}
  }`

	tokens, err := caddyfile.Tokenize([]byte(blockContent), "test.caddyfile")
	if err != nil {
		panic(err)
	}
	
	fmt.Println("Tokens for directive block:")
	for i, token := range tokens {
		fmt.Printf("%d: %q (line %d)\n", i, token.Text, token.Line)
	}
	
	// Simulate what the parser does
	bd := caddyfile.NewDispenser(tokens)
	fmt.Println("\nSimulating parser logic:")
	
	for bd.Next() {
		fmt.Printf("Current token: %q\n", bd.Val())
		
		// This is the problematic check
		if bd.Val() == "{" {
			fmt.Println("ERROR: anonymous blocks are not supported")
			break
		}
		
		fmt.Printf("Current mapping key: %q\n", bd.Val())
		
		// Try to read arguments
		args := []string{}
		for bd.NextArg() {
			args = append(args, bd.Val())
		}
		fmt.Printf("Arguments: %v\n", args)
	}
}'

Now I understand the issue! Looking at the problematic code in `/testbed/caddyconfig/caddyfile/parse.go` around line 385-387, the code is checking if a token value is `"{"` and if so, it returns an error saying "anonymous blocks are not supported". 

However, this check is happening too early and incorrectly. When parsing an import block like:
```caddyfile
import site test.domain {
  reverse_proxy http://192.168.1.1:8080 { 
    header_up Host {host}
    header_up X-Real-IP {remote_host}
  }
}
```

The block tokens that are extracted contain the directive `reverse_proxy` followed by its arguments and then a block `{ ... }`. The current code sees the `{` token and incorrectly treats it as an anonymous block, when in fact it's a perfectly valid block for the `reverse_proxy` directive.

The fix should allow legitimate blocks within directives in import blocks, while still preventing truly anonymous blocks that start with `{`.

Let me analyze the logic more carefully

Based on my analysis, I understand the issue now. The problem is that when parsing an import block that starts with a directive followed by a block (like `reverse_proxy { ... }`), the code is incorrectly treating this as an "anonymous block" rather than recognizing it as a directive with block contents.

Looking at the problematic code around line 385-386, when `bd.Val() == "{"`, it returns an error saying "anonymous blocks are not supported". However, this is not actually an anonymous block - it's a directive block that's correctly structured within the import block.

The issue is that the code is trying to treat each line in the import block as if it should start with a mapping key, but directives within import blocks can legitimately have arguments that include blocks.

Let me examine how the snippet "site" is defined and how the block replacement should work

   525

   531	                                maybeSnippetId = false

   542	                var tokensToAdd []Token
   543	                switch {

   545	                        tokensToAdd = blockTokens
   546	                case strings.HasPrefix(token.Text, "{blocks.") && strings.HasSuffix(token.Text, "}"):
   547	                        // {blocks.foo.bar} will be extracted to key `foo.bar`
   548	                        blockKey := strings.TrimPrefix(strings.TrimSuffix(token.Text, "}"), "{blocks.")

2026-01-08 09:44:02,239 - INFO - swea-agent - 💭 THOUGHT
Now I understand the issue completely. The problem is in the `doImport` function where it's trying to parse the block content after an import directive. The code is trying to create a `blockMapping` for placeholder replacement, but it's incorrectly rejecting legitimate directive blocks.

Looking at the snippet definition:
```caddyfile
(site) {
  http://{args[0]} https://{args[0]} {
    {block}
  }
}
```

The `{block}` placeholder should be replaced with the content of the import block. However, when the import block contains a directive with its own nested block (like `reverse_proxy` with `{ ... }`), the current code incorrectly treats this as an "anonymous block".

The fix is to modify the logic in the `doImport` function to properly handle directive blocks within import blocks. The current check at line 385-386 is too restrictive.

Let me implement the fix:

🎬 ACTION
str_replace_editor str_replace /testbed/caddyconfig/caddyfile/parse.go   --old_str '	if len(blockTokens) > 0 {
		// use such tokens to create a new dispenser, and then use it to parse each block
		bd := NewDispenser(blockTokens)
		for bd.Next() {
			// see if we can grab a key
			var currentMappingKey string
			if bd.Val() == "{" {
				return p.Err("anonymous blocks are not supported")
			}
			currentMappingKey = bd.Val()
			currentMappingTokens := []Token{}
			// read all args until end of line / {
			if bd.NextArg() {
				currentMappingTokens = append(currentMappingTokens, bd.Token())
				for bd.NextArg() {
					currentMappingTokens = append(currentMappingTokens, bd.Token())
				}
				// TODO(elee1766): we don'"'"'t enter another mapping here because it'"'"'s annoying to extract the { and } properly.
				// maybe someone can do that in the future
			} else {
				// attempt to enter a block and add tokens to the currentMappingTokens
				for mappingNesting := bd.Nesting(); bd.NextBlock(mappingNesting); {
					currentMappingTokens = append(currentMappingTokens, bd.Token())
				}
			}
			blockMapping[currentMappingKey] = currentMappingTokens
		}
	}' --new_str '	if len(blockTokens) > 0 {

func main() {

import (
	"fmt"
)

func main() {
	// Simulate the nesting behavior
	testCases := []struct {
		description string
		tokens      []string
	}{
		{
			description: "Simple directive with block",
			tokens:      []string{"reverse_proxy", "http://192.168.1.1:8080", "{", "header_up", "Host", "{host}", "header_up", "X-Real-IP", "{remote_host}", "}"},
		},
	}

	for _, tc := range testCases {
		fmt.Printf("Test case: %s\n", tc.description)
		fmt.Println("Tokens:", tc.tokens)
		
		// Simulate what happens in the parser
		nesting := 0
		for i, token := range tc.tokens {
			fmt.Printf("Token %d: %q", i, token)
			if token == "{" {
				nesting++
				fmt.Printf(" -> nesting++ = %d", nesting)
			} else if token == "}" {
				nesting--
				fmt.Printf(" -> nesting-- = %d", nesting)
			}
			fmt.Println()
		}
		fmt.Println()
	}
}'

import (
	"fmt"
)

func main() {
	// Simulate the nesting behavior
	testCases := []struct {
		description string
		tokens      []string
	}{
		{
			description: "Simple directive with block",
			tokens:      []string{"reverse_proxy", "http://192.168.1.1:8080", "{", "header_up", "Host", "{host}", "header_up", "X-Real-IP", "{remote_host}", "}"},
		},
	}

	for _, tc := range testCases {
		fmt.Printf("Test case: %s\n", tc.description)
		fmt.Println("Tokens:", tc.tokens)
		
		// Simulate what happens in the parser
		nesting := 0
		for i, token := range tc.tokens {
			fmt.Printf("Token %d: %q", i, token)
			if token == "{" {
				nesting++
				fmt.Printf(" -> nesting++ = %d", nesting)
			} else if token == "}" {
				nesting--
				fmt.Printf(" -> nesting-- = %d", nesting)
			}
			fmt.Println()
		}
		fmt.Println()
	}
}'


The issue is still occurring. Let me analyze the problem more carefully. The problem is that my fix is not addressing the root cause. Let me think about this differently.

The issue is that when parsing the import block, the code is trying to create a `blockMapping` for placeholder replacement. The current logic assumes that each line in the import block should start with a mapping key, but when a directive has a nested block, it starts with `{`.

However, looking at the code more carefully, I think the real issue is that the code is trying to parse the import block content as a mapping, but it should allow for directives that contain their own blocks.

Let me examine what should happen. The snippet definition is:
```caddyfile
(site) {
  http://{args[0]} https://{args[0]} {
    {block}
  }
}
```

When we import it with:
```caddyfile
import site test.domain {
  reverse_proxy http://192.168.1.1:8080 { 
    header_up Host {host}
    header_up X-Real-IP {remote_host}
  }
}
```

The `{block}` placeholder should be replaced by the entire content of the import block. The current code is trying to parse each line as a mapping key-value pair, but it should treat the entire block content as a single unit to replace the placeholder.

Let me look at how the replacement is supposed to work:

   542	                var tokensToAdd []Token
   543	                switch {
   544	                case token.Text == "{block}":
   545	                        tokensToAdd = blockTokens
   546	                case strings.HasPrefix(token.Text, "{blocks.") && strings.HasSuffix(token.Text, "}"):
   547	                        // {blocks.foo.bar} will be extracted to key `foo.bar`
   548	                        blockKey := strings.TrimPrefix(strings.TrimSuffix(token.Text, "}"), "{blocks.")

2026-01-08 09:51:22,809 - INFO - swea-agent - 💭 THOUGHT
I see the issue now. The problem is that the code is trying to parse the import block content as individual key-value mappings, but when a directive has a nested block, it should be treated as a single unit.

Looking at the code, when `{block}` is encountered in a snippet, it should be replaced with all the `blockTokens` (line 545). The issue is that the code is trying to create a more granular `blockMapping` but it's incorrectly rejecting blocks within directives.

The real problem is that the code at lines 382-405 is attempting to parse the import block content as individual mappings, but this is fundamentally wrong when the content contains directives with their own blocks.

The correct fix is to remove the logic that tries to parse the import block as individual mappings and just treat the entire block content as a single unit for the `{block}` placeholder. Let me implement this fix:

🎬 ACTION

	var blockTokens []Token
	for currentNesting := p.Nesting(); p.NextBlock(currentNesting); {
		blockTokens = append(blockTokens, p.Token())
	}
	// initialize with size 1
	blockMapping := make(map[string][]Token, 1)
	if len(blockTokens) > 0 {
		// use such tokens to create a new dispenser, and then use it to parse each block
		bd := NewDispenser(blockTokens)
		for bd.Next() {
			// see if we can grab a key
			var currentMappingKey string
			if bd.Val() == "{" && bd.Nesting() == 0 {
				return p.Err("anonymous blocks are not supported")
			}
			currentMappingKey = bd.Val()
			currentMappingTokens := []Token{}
			// read all args until end of line / {
			if bd.NextArg() {
				currentMappingTokens = append(currentMappingTokens, bd.Token())

					currentMappingTokens = append(currentMappingTokens, bd.Token())
				}

				// maybe someone can do that in the future
			} else {

					currentMappingTokens = append(currentMappingTokens, bd.Token())
				}
			}
			blockMapping[currentMappingKey] = currentMappingTokens
		}

2026-01-08 09:53:30,468 - DEBUG - swea-lm - total_tokens_sent=0, total_tokens_received=3,290, total_cost=0.00, total_api_calls=52
2026-01-08 09:53:30,477 - INFO - swea-agent - 💭 THOUGHT
I've analyzed the issue and have a solution. The problem is that the parser is incorrectly flagging directives with blocks as "anonymous blocks not supported" when they appear as part of an import statement's block content.

The key insight is that the error check on line 385-386 is too restrictive. It's designed to prevent anonymous blocks like `{ ... }` but it's incorrectly triggering on legitimate directives that contain blocks like `reverse_proxy { ... }`.

The actual issue is that when parsing the block content after an import directive, the code is trying to parse individual directives and arguments, but it doesn't handle the case where a directive has its own block properly. Instead of trying to extract individual mappings, we should simply store the entire block content as-is for `{block}` replacement.

Let me make the fix:



🎬 ACTION

	}
	// initialize with size 1

	if len(blockTokens) > 0 {
		// use such tokens to create a new dispenser, and then use it to parse each block
		bd := NewDispenser(blockTokens)

			// see if we can grab a key
			var currentMappingKey string
			if bd.Val() == "{" && bd.Nesting() == 0 {
				return p.Err("anonymous blocks are not supported")
			}
			currentMappingKey = bd.Val()

			// read all args until end of line / {

				currentMappingTokens = append(currentMappingTokens, bd.Token())

				}
			}
			blockMapping[currentMappingKey] = currentMappingTokens
		}

+                        continue

+                envParts := strings.SplitN(string(envString), envVarDefaultDelimiter, 2)
+
+                // do a lookup for the env var, replace with the default if not found
+                envVarValue, found := os.LookupEnv(envParts[0])
+                if !found && len(envParts) == 2 {
+                        envVarValue = envParts[1]
+                }
+
+                // get the value of the environment variable
+                // note that this causes one-level deep chaining
+                envVarBytes := []byte(envVarValue)
+
+                // splice in the value
+                input = append(input[:begin],
+                        append(envVarBytes, input[end+len(spanClose):]...)...)
+
+                // continue at the end of the replacement
+                offset = begin + len(envVarBytes)
+        }
+        return input

+                // Reject request matchers if trying to define them globally
+                if strings.HasPrefix(value, "@") {
+                        return p.Errf("request matchers may not be defined globally, they must be in a site block; found %s", value)
+                }
+
+                // Special case: import directive replaces tokens during parse-time
+                if value == "import" && p.isNewLine() {
+                        err := p.doImport(0)
+                        if err != nil {
+                                return err
+                        }
+                        continue
+                }
+
+                // Open brace definitely indicates end of addresses
+                if value == "{" {
+                        if expectingAnother {
+                                return p.Errf("Expected another address but had '%s' - check for extra comma", value)
+                        }
+                        // Mark this server block as being defined with braces.
+                        // This is used to provide a better error message when
+                        // the user may have tried to define two server blocks
+                        // without having used braces, which are required in
+                        // that case.
+                        p.block.HasBraces = true
+                        break
+                }
+
+                // Users commonly forget to place a space between the address and the '{'
+                if strings.HasSuffix(value, "{") {
+                        return p.Errf("Site addresses cannot end with a curly brace: '%s' - put a space between the token and the brace", value)
+                }
+
+                if value != "" { // empty token possible if user typed ""
+                        // Trailing comma indicates another address will follow, which
+                        // may possibly be on the next line
+                        if value[len(value)-1] == ',' {
+                                value = value[:len(value)-1]
+                                expectingAnother = true
+                        } else {
+                                expectingAnother = false // but we may still see another one on this line
+                        }
+
+                        // If there's a comma here, it's probably because they didn't use a space
+                        // between their two domains, e.g. "foo.com,bar.com", which would not be
+                        // parsed as two separate site addresses.
+                        if strings.Contains(value, ",") {
+                                return p.Errf("Site addresses cannot contain a comma ',': '%s' - put a space after the comma to separate site addresses", value)
+                        }
+
+                        // After the above, a comma surrounded by spaces would result
+                        // in an empty token which we should ignore
+                        if value != "" {
+                                // Add the token as a site address
+                                token.Text = value
+                                p.block.Keys = append(p.block.Keys, token)
+                        }
+                }
+
+                // Advance token and possibly break out of loop or return error
+                hasNext := p.Next()
+                if expectingAnother && !hasNext {
+                        return p.EOFErr()
+                }
+                if !hasNext {
+                        p.eof = true
+                        break // EOF
+                }
+                if !expectingAnother && p.isNewLine() {
+                        break
+                }
+        }
+
+        return nil
 }

+                p.cursor--
+        }

 }

+        repl := makeArgsReplacer(args)

+        // grab all the tokens (if it exists) from within a block that follows the import
+        var blockTokens []Token
+        for currentNesting := p.Nesting(); p.NextBlock(currentNesting); {
+                blockTokens = append(blockTokens, p.Token())
+        }
+        // initialize with size 1
+        blockMapping := make(map[string][]Token, 1)
+        if len(blockTokens) > 0 {
+                // use such tokens to create a new dispenser, and then use it to parse each block
+                bd := NewDispenser(blockTokens)
+                for bd.Next() {
+                        // see if we can grab a key
+                        var currentMappingKey string
+                        if bd.Val() == "{" && bd.Nesting() == 0 {
+                                return p.Err("anonymous blocks are not supported")
+                        }
+                        currentMappingKey = bd.Val()

+                        // read all args until end of line / {
+                        if bd.NextArg() {
+                                currentMappingTokens = append(currentMappingTokens, bd.Token())
+                                for bd.NextArg() {
+                                        currentMappingTokens = append(currentMappingTokens, bd.Token())
+                                }
+                                // TODO(elee1766): we don't enter another mapping here because it's annoying to extract the { and } properly.
+                                // maybe someone can do that in the future
+                        } else {
+                                // attempt to enter a block and add tokens to the currentMappingTokens
+                                for mappingNesting := bd.Nesting(); bd.NextBlock(mappingNesting); {
+                                        currentMappingTokens = append(currentMappingTokens, bd.Token())
+                                }
+                        }
+                        blockMapping[currentMappingKey] = currentMappingTokens
+                }
+        }
+
+        // splice out the import directive and its arguments
+        // (2 tokens, plus the length of args)
+        tokensBefore := p.tokens[:p.cursor-1-len(args)-len(blockTokens)]
+        tokensAfter := p.tokens[p.cursor+1:]
+        var importedTokens []Token
+        var nodes []string
+
+        // first check snippets. That is a simple, non-recursive replacement
+        if p.definedSnippets != nil && p.definedSnippets[importPattern] != nil {
+                importedTokens = p.definedSnippets[importPattern]
+                if len(importedTokens) > 0 {
+                        // just grab the first one
+                        nodes = append(nodes, fmt.Sprintf("%s:%s", importedTokens[0].File, importedTokens[0].snippetName))
+                }
+        } else {
+                // make path relative to the file of the _token_ being processed rather
+                // than current working directory (issue #867) and then use glob to get
+                // list of matching filenames
+                absFile, err := caddy.FastAbs(p.Dispenser.File())
+                if err != nil {
+                        return p.Errf("Failed to get absolute path of file: %s: %v", p.Dispenser.File(), err)
+                }
+
+                var matches []string
+                var globPattern string
+                if !filepath.IsAbs(importPattern) {
+                        globPattern = filepath.Join(filepath.Dir(absFile), importPattern)
+                } else {
+                        globPattern = importPattern
+                }
+                if strings.Count(globPattern, "*") > 1 || strings.Count(globPattern, "?") > 1 ||
+                        (strings.Contains(globPattern, "[") && strings.Contains(globPattern, "]")) {
+                        // See issue #2096 - a pattern with many glob expansions can hang for too long
+                        return p.Errf("Glob pattern may only contain one wildcard (*), but has others: %s", globPattern)
+                }
+                matches, err = filepath.Glob(globPattern)
+                if err != nil {
+                        return p.Errf("Failed to use import pattern %s: %v", importPattern, err)
+                }
+                if len(matches) == 0 {
+                        if strings.ContainsAny(globPattern, "*?[]") {
+                                caddy.Log().Warn("No files matching import glob pattern", zap.String("pattern", importPattern))
+                        } else {
+                                return p.Errf("File to import not found: %s", importPattern)
+                        }
+                } else {
+                        // See issue #5295 - should skip any files that start with a . when iterating over them.
+                        sep := string(filepath.Separator)
+                        segGlobPattern := strings.Split(globPattern, sep)
+                        if strings.HasPrefix(segGlobPattern[len(segGlobPattern)-1], "*") {
+                                var tmpMatches []string
+                                for _, m := range matches {
+                                        seg := strings.Split(m, sep)
+                                        if !strings.HasPrefix(seg[len(seg)-1], ".") {
+                                                tmpMatches = append(tmpMatches, m)
+                                        }
+                                }
+                                matches = tmpMatches
+                        }
+                }
+
+                // collect all the imported tokens
+                for _, importFile := range matches {
+                        newTokens, err := p.doSingleImport(importFile)
+                        if err != nil {
+                                return err
+                        }
+                        importedTokens = append(importedTokens, newTokens...)
+                }
+                nodes = matches
+        }
+
+        nodeName := p.File()
+        if p.Token().snippetName != "" {
+                nodeName += fmt.Sprintf(":%s", p.Token().snippetName)
+        }
+        p.importGraph.addNode(nodeName)
+        p.importGraph.addNodes(nodes)
+        if err := p.importGraph.addEdges(nodeName, nodes); err != nil {
+                p.importGraph.removeNodes(nodes)
+                return err
+        }
+
+        // copy the tokens so we don't overwrite p.definedSnippets
+        tokensCopy := make([]Token, 0, len(importedTokens))
+
+        var (
+                maybeSnippet   bool
+                maybeSnippetId bool
+                index          int
+        )
+
+        // run the argument replacer on the tokens
+        // golang for range slice return a copy of value
+        // similarly, append also copy value
+        for i, token := range importedTokens {
+                // update the token's imports to refer to import directive filename, line number and snippet name if there is one
+                if token.snippetName != "" {
+                        token.imports = append(token.imports, fmt.Sprintf("%s:%d (import %s)", p.File(), p.Line(), token.snippetName))
+                } else {
+                        token.imports = append(token.imports, fmt.Sprintf("%s:%d (import)", p.File(), p.Line()))
+                }
+
+                // naive way of determine snippets, as snippets definition can only follow name + block
+                // format, won't check for nesting correctness or any other error, that's what parser does.
+                if !maybeSnippet && nesting == 0 {
+                        // first of the line
+                        if i == 0 || isNextOnNewLine(tokensCopy[i-1], token) {
+                                index = 0
+                        } else {
+                                index++
+                        }
+
+                        if index == 0 && len(token.Text) >= 3 && strings.HasPrefix(token.Text, "(") && strings.HasSuffix(token.Text, ")") {
+                                maybeSnippetId = true
+                        }
+                }
+
+                switch token.Text {
+                case "{":
+                        nesting++
+                        if index == 1 && maybeSnippetId && nesting == 1 {
+                                maybeSnippet = true
+                                maybeSnippetId = false
+                        }
+                case "}":
+                        nesting--
+                        if nesting == 0 && maybeSnippet {
+                                maybeSnippet = false
+                        }
+                }
+                // if it is {block}, we substitute with all tokens in the block
+                // if it is {blocks.*}, we substitute with the tokens in the mapping for the *
+                var skip bool
+                var tokensToAdd []Token
+                switch {
+                case token.Text == "{block}":
+                        tokensToAdd = blockTokens
+                case strings.HasPrefix(token.Text, "{blocks.") && strings.HasSuffix(token.Text, "}"):
+                        // {blocks.foo.bar} will be extracted to key `foo.bar`
+                        blockKey := strings.TrimPrefix(strings.TrimSuffix(token.Text, "}"), "{blocks.")
+                        val, ok := blockMapping[blockKey]
+                        if ok {
+                                tokensToAdd = val
+                        }
+                default:
+                        skip = true
+                }
+                if !skip {
+                        if len(tokensToAdd) == 0 {
+                                // if there is no content in the snippet block, don't do any replacement
+                                // this allows snippets which contained {block}/{block.*} before this change to continue functioning as normal
+                                tokensCopy = append(tokensCopy, token)
+                        } else {
+                                tokensCopy = append(tokensCopy, tokensToAdd...)
+                        }
+                        continue
+                }
+
+                if maybeSnippet {
+                        tokensCopy = append(tokensCopy, token)
+                        continue
+                }
+
+                foundVariadic, startIndex, endIndex := parseVariadic(token, len(args))
+                if foundVariadic {
+                        for _, arg := range args[startIndex:endIndex] {
+                                token.Text = arg
+                                tokensCopy = append(tokensCopy, token)
+                        }
+                } else {
+                        token.Text = repl.ReplaceKnown(token.Text, "")
+                        tokensCopy = append(tokensCopy, token)
+                }
+        }
+
+        // splice the imported tokens in the place of the import statement
+        // and rewind cursor so Next() will land on first imported token
+        p.tokens = append(tokensBefore, append(tokensCopy, tokensAfter...)...)
+        p.cursor -= len(args) + len(blockTokens) + 1
+
+        return nil
 }

+        // variables before we parse, which changes the underlying array (#4422)
+        inputCopy := make([]byte, len(input))
+        copy(inputCopy, input)
+
+        tokens, err := allTokens(filename, inputCopy)
+        if err != nil {
+                return nil, err
+        }
+        p := parser{
+                Dispenser: NewDispenser(tokens),
+                importGraph: importGraph{
+                        nodes: make(map[string]struct{}),
+                        edges: make(adjacency),
+                },
+        }
+        return p.parseAll()
 }

 // It mutates the underlying array and returns the updated slice.
 func replaceEnvVars(input []byte) []byte {

-		}
-		end += begin + len(spanOpen) // make end relative to input, not begin
-
-		// get the name; if there is no name, skip it
-		envString := input[begin+len(spanOpen) : end]
-		if len(envString) == 0 {
-			offset = end + len(spanClose)
-			continue
-		}
-
-		// split the string into a key and an optional default
-		envParts := strings.SplitN(string(envString), envVarDefaultDelimiter, 2)
-
-		// do a lookup for the env var, replace with the default if not found

+        var offset int
+        for {
+                begin := bytes.Index(input[offset:], spanOpen)
+                if begin < 0 {
+                        break
+                }
+                begin += offset // make beginning relative to input, not offset
+                end := bytes.Index(input[begin+len(spanOpen):], spanClose)
+                if end < 0 {
+                        break
+                }
+                end += begin + len(spanOpen) // make end relative to input, not begin
+
+                // get the name; if there is no name, skip it
+                envString := input[begin+len(spanOpen) : end]
+                if len(envString) == 0 {
+                        offset = end + len(spanClose)
+                        continue
+                }
+
+                // split the string into a key and an optional default
+                envParts := strings.SplitN(string(envString), envVarDefaultDelimiter, 2)
+
+                // do a lookup for the env var, replace with the default if not found
+                envVarValue, found := os.LookupEnv(envParts[0])
+                if !found && len(envParts) == 2 {
+                        envVarValue = envParts[1]
+                }
+
+                // get the value of the environment variable
+                // note that this causes one-level deep chaining
+                envVarBytes := []byte(envVarValue)
+
+                // splice in the value
+                input = append(input[:begin],
+                        append(envVarBytes, input[end+len(spanClose):]...)...)
+
+                // continue at the end of the replacement
+                offset = begin + len(envVarBytes)
+        }
+        return input
 }

+        var expectingAnother bool

+        for {
+                value := p.Val()

+                // Reject request matchers if trying to define them globally

+                }

+                // Special case: import directive replaces tokens during parse-time
+                if value == "import" && p.isNewLine() {
+                        err := p.doImport(0)
+                        if err != nil {
+                                return err
+                        }
+                        continue
+                }
+
+                // Open brace definitely indicates end of addresses
+                if value == "{" {
+                        if expectingAnother {
+                                return p.Errf("Expected another address but had '%s' - check for extra comma", value)
+                        }
+                        // Mark this server block as being defined with braces.
+                        // This is used to provide a better error message when
+                        // the user may have tried to define two server blocks
+                        // without having used braces, which are required in
+                        // that case.
+                        p.block.HasBraces = true
+                        break
+                }
+
+                // Users commonly forget to place a space between the address and the '{'
+                if strings.HasSuffix(value, "{") {
+                        return p.Errf("Site addresses cannot end with a curly brace: '%s' - put a space between the token and the brace", value)
+                }
+
+                if value != "" { // empty token possible if user typed ""
+                        // Trailing comma indicates another address will follow, which
+                        // may possibly be on the next line
+                        if value[len(value)-1] == ',' {
+                                value = value[:len(value)-1]
+                                expectingAnother = true
+                        } else {
+                                expectingAnother = false // but we may still see another one on this line
+                        }
+
+                        // If there's a comma here, it's probably because they didn't use a space
+                        // between their two domains, e.g. "foo.com,bar.com", which would not be
+                        // parsed as two separate site addresses.
+                        if strings.Contains(value, ",") {
+                                return p.Errf("Site addresses cannot contain a comma ',': '%s' - put a space after the comma to separate site addresses", value)
+                        }
+
+                        // After the above, a comma surrounded by spaces would result
+                        // in an empty token which we should ignore
+                        if value != "" {
+                                // Add the token as a site address
+                                token.Text = value
+                                p.block.Keys = append(p.block.Keys, token)
+                        }
+                }
+
+                // Advance token and possibly break out of loop or return error
+                hasNext := p.Next()
+                if expectingAnother && !hasNext {
+                        return p.EOFErr()
+                }
+                if !hasNext {
+                        p.eof = true
+                        break // EOF
+                }
+                if !expectingAnother && p.isNewLine() {
+                        break
+                }
+        }
+
+        return nil
 }
